<BRK />
<SCN>SECTION 03 30 00</SCN><BRK />
<STL><pre class="display_STL">&lt;STL&gt;</pre>CAST-IN-PLACE CONCRETE<pre class="display_STL">&lt;/STL&gt;</pre></STL><BRK />
<DTE>02/19</DTE><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: This guide specification has been edited to cover the minimum requirements and include Japanese products, 
where feasible, for a standard Japan Engineer District project. The Designer of Record (DOR) shall tailor as 
applicable to meet project specific requirements.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: This guide specification covers the requirements for <SCP>cast-in-place concrete not exposed to a marine or 
high chloride environment</SCP>. For concrete exposed to a marine or high chloride environment, use Section 
<SRF><pre class="display_SRF">&lt;SRF&gt;</pre>03 31 30<pre class="display_SRF">&lt;/SRF&gt;</pre></SRF> MARINE CONCRETE.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>Adhere to <URL HREF="http://www.wbdg.org/ffc/dod/unified-facilities-criteria-ufc/ufc-1-300-02">UFC 1-300-02</URL> Unified Facilities Guide Specifications (UFGS) Format Standard when editing this guide 
specification or preparing new project specification sections. Edit this guide specification for project specific 
requirements by adding, deleting, or revising text. For bracketed items, choose applicable item(s) or insert 
appropriate information.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>Remove information and requirements not required in respective project, whether or not brackets are present.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>Comments, suggestions and recommended changes for this guide specification are welcome and should be submitted 
as a <URL HREF="http://www.wbdg.org/ffc/dod/unified-facilities-guide-specifications-ufgs">Criteria Change Request (CCR)</URL>.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: Show the following information on the project drawings:<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>1. Loading assumptions.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>2. Assumed temperature range when temperature stresses are a factor in design.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>3. Material strengths used in design for each element, f'c.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>4. Yield strength of reinforcement required<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> per JIS G 3112<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET>.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>5. Details of concrete sections, showing dimensions, reinforcement cover, and required camber.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>6. Locations where structural lightweight concrete or lightweight insulation or fill concrete are used.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>7. Details which require a depressed structural slab for static-disseminating and spark-resistant tile, terrazzo, 
or other floor finishes in order to provide finished surfaces at the same elevations.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>8. Indicate the locations in the finished structure, when exposed concrete surfaces are specified. Indicate the 
type and location, if other than cast finish is required.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>

</SPT><SPT outline="1.2"><TTL>DEFINITIONS</TTL><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">a. "Cementitious material" as used herein must include all portland cement, pozzolan, fly ash, and slag cement.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">b. "Exposed to public view" means situated so that it can be seen from eye level from a public location after completion of the building. 
A public location is accessible to persons not responsible for operation or maintenance of the building.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">c. "Chemical admixtures" are materials in the form of powder or fluids that are added to the concrete to give it certain characteristics 
not obtainable with plain concrete mixes.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">d. "Supplementary cementing materials" (SCM) include coal fly ash, slag cement, natural or calcined pozzolans, and ultra-fine coal ash 
when used in such proportions to replace the portland cement that result in improvement to sustainability and durability and reduced cost.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">e. "Design strength" (f'c) is the specified compressive strength of concrete at time(s) specified in this section to meet structural design 
criteria.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">f. "Mass Concrete" is any concrete system that approaches a maximum temperature of<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 70 degrees C<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 158 degrees F<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> within the first 72 hours 
of placement. In addition, it includes all concrete elements with a section thickness of<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 1 meter<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 3 feet<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> or more regardless of temperature.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">g. "Mixture proportioning" is the process of designing concrete mixture proportions to enable it to meet the strength, service life and 
constructability requirements of the project while minimizing the initial and life-cycle cost.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">h. "Mixture proportions" are the masses or volumes of individual ingredients used to make a unit measure (cubic meter or cubic yard) of 
concrete.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">i. "Pozzolan" is a siliceous or siliceous and aluminous material, which in itself possesses little or no cementitious value but will, 
in finely divided form and in the presence of moisture, chemically react with calcium hydroxide at ordinary temperatures to form compounds 
possessing cementitious properties.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">j. "Workability (or consistence)" is the ability of a fresh (plastic) concrete mix to fill the form/mould properly with the desired work 
(vibration) and without reducing the concrete's quality. Workability depends on water content, chemical admixtures, aggregate (shape and 
size distribution), cementitious content and age (level of hydration).</LST><BRK /></SPT>

<TXT>Accomplish work in accordance with <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JASS 5<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> and <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>MLIT-SS Chapter 6<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> or ACI publications except as modified herein. Consider the advisory or recommended 
provisions to be mandatory. Interpret reference to the "Building Official," the "Structural Engineer," and the "Architect/Engineer" to mean the 
Contracting Officer.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
<SPT outline="1.5"><TTL>DELIVERY, STORAGE, AND HANDLING</TTL><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: Materials which are woven, fibrous, or porous in nature have a high capacity to adsorb VOC emissions; for 
instance, acoustical ceilings, carpet, textiles, and unprimed gypsum wall board.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<TXT>Follow <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JASS 5<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> and <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>MLIT-SS Chapter 6<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>, requirements and recommendations. Do not deliver concrete until vapor retarder, <div class="brackets">[vapor barrier,]</div> forms, reinforcement, 
embedded items, and chamfer strips are in place and ready for concrete placement. Do not store concrete curing compounds or sealers with materials 
that have a high capacity to adsorb volatile organic compound (VOC) emissions, including <div class="brackets">[_____]</div>. Do not store concrete curing compounds or sealers 
in occupied spaces.</TXT><BRK />
<SPT outline="1.5.1"><TTL>Reinforcement</TTL><BRK />
<TXT>Store reinforcement of different sizes and shapes in separate piles or racks raised above the ground to avoid excessive rusting. Protect from 
contaminants such as grease, oil, and dirt. Ensure bar sizes can be accurately identified after bundles are broken and tags removed.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
</SPT><SPT outline="1.6"><TTL>QUALITY ASSURANCE</TTL><BRK />
<SPT outline="1.6.1"><TTL>Design Data</TTL><BRK />
<SPT outline="1.6.1.1"><TTL><SUB><pre class="display_SUB">&lt;SUB&gt;</pre>Concrete Mix Design<pre class="display_SUB">&lt;/SUB&gt;</pre></SUB></TTL><BRK />
<TXT>Sixty days minimum prior to concrete placement, submit a mix design for each strength and type of concrete. Submit a complete list of materials 
including type; brand; source and amount of cement, supplementary cementitious materials, <div class="brackets">[fibers]</div>, and admixtures; and applicable reference specifications. 
Submit mill test and all other test for cement, supplementary cementitious materials, aggregates, and admixtures. Provide documentation of maximum 
nominal aggregate size, gradation analysis, percentage retained and passing sieve, and a graph of percentage retained verses sieve size. Provide 
mix proportion data using at least three different water-cementitious material ratios for each type of mixture, which produce a range of strength 
encompassing those required for each type of concrete required. If source material changes, resubmit mix proportion data using revised source 
material. Provide only materials that have been proven by trial mix studies to meet the requirements of this specification, unless otherwise approved 
in writing by the Contracting Officer. Indicate clearly in the submittal where each mix design is used when more than one mix design is submitted. 
Resubmit data on concrete components if the qualities or source of components changes. For previously approved concrete mix designs used within 
the past twelve months, the previous mix design may be re-submitted without further trial batch testing if accompanied by material test data conducted 
within the last six months. Obtain mix design approval from the contracting officer prior to concrete placement.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
</SPT><SPT outline="1.6.2"><TTL>Shop Drawings</TTL><BRK />
<SPT outline="1.6.2.1"><TTL><SUB><pre class="display_SUB">&lt;SUB&gt;</pre>Reinforcing Steel<pre class="display_SUB">&lt;/SUB&gt;</pre></SUB></TTL><BRK />
<TXT>Indicate bending diagrams, assembly diagrams, splicing and laps of bars, shapes, dimensions, and details of bar reinforcing, accessories, and concrete 
cover. Do not scale dimensions from structural drawings to determine lengths of reinforcing bars. Reproductions of contract drawings are unacceptable.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
</SPT><SPT outline="1.6.3"><TTL>Control Submittals</TTL><BRK />
<div class="brackets">[<SPT outline="1.6.3.1"><TTL><SUB><pre class="display_SUB">&lt;SUB&gt;</pre>Concrete Curing Plan<pre class="display_SUB">&lt;/SUB&gt;</pre></SUB></TTL><BRK />
<TXT>Submit proposed materials, methods and duration for curing concrete elements in accordance with <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JASS 5<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> and <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>MLIT-SS Chapter 6<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
]</div><div class="brackets">[<SPT outline="1.6.3.2"><TTL><SUB><pre class="display_SUB">&lt;SUB&gt;</pre>Pumping Concrete<pre class="display_SUB">&lt;/SUB&gt;</pre></SUB></TTL><BRK />
<TXT>Submit proposed materials and methods for pumping concrete. Submittal must include mix designs, pumping equipment including type of pump and size 
and material for pipe, and maximum length and height concrete is to be pumped.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
]</div><div class="brackets">[<SPT outline="1.6.3.3"><TTL><SUB><pre class="display_SUB">&lt;SUB&gt;</pre>Finishing Plan<pre class="display_SUB">&lt;/SUB&gt;</pre></SUB></TTL><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: Include when finishing or special flatness are critical.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<TXT>Submit proposed material and procedures to be used in obtaining the finish for the <div class="brackets">[_____]</div> floors. Include qualification of person to be used 
for obtaining floor tolerance measurement, description of measuring equipment to be used, and a sketch showing lines and locations the measuring 
equipment will follow.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
]</div><div class="brackets">[<SPT outline="1.6.3.4"><TTL><SUB><pre class="display_SUB">&lt;SUB&gt;</pre>VOC Content for form release agents, curing compounds, and concrete penetrating sealers<pre class="display_SUB">&lt;/SUB&gt;</pre></SUB></TTL><BRK />
<TXT>Submit certification for the form release agent, curing compounds, and concrete penetrating sealers that indicate the VOC content of each product.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
]</div><SPT outline="1.6.3.5"><TTL><SUB><pre class="display_SUB">&lt;SUB&gt;</pre>Safety Data Sheets<pre class="display_SUB">&lt;/SUB&gt;</pre></SUB></TTL><BRK />

work shift to employees when they are at the construction site.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>

]</div></SPT><SPT outline="1.6.6"><TTL><SUB><pre class="display_SUB">&lt;SUB&gt;</pre>Quality Control Plan<pre class="display_SUB">&lt;/SUB&gt;</pre></SUB></TTL><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: The objective of the concrete quality control program is for the Contractor to outline the procedures that 
will be used to construct a structure that will obtain the design service life.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<TXT>Develop and submit for approval a concrete quality control program in accordance with the guidelines of <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JASS 5<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> and <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>MLIT-SS Chapter 6<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> and as specified 
herein. The plan must include approved laboratories. Provide direct oversight for the concrete qualification program inclusive of associated sampling 
and testing. All quality control reports must be provided to the Contracting Officer, Quality Manager and Concrete Supplier.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
<SPT outline="1.6.7"><TTL>Quality Control Personnel Certifications</TTL><BRK />
<TXT>The Contractor must submit for approval the responsibilities of the various quality control personnel, including the names and qualifications of 
the individuals in those positions and a quality control organizational chart defining the quality control hierarchy and the responsibility of 
the various positions. Quality control personnel must be employed by the Contractor.</TXT><BRK />
<TXT>Submit Japan Concrete Institute (JCI) or American Concrete Institute (ACI) certification for the following:</TXT><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">a. CQC personnel responsible for inspection of concrete operations.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">b. Lead Foreman or Journeyman of the Concrete Placing, Finishing, and Curing Crews.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">c. Field Testing Technicians: ACI Concrete Field Testing Technician, Grade I or equivalent Japan Concrete Institute (JCI) Concrete Field 
Testing Technician.</LST><BRK />
<SPT outline="1.6.7.1"><TTL>Quality Manager Qualifications</TTL><BRK />
<TXT>The quality manager must hold a current license as a First Class Kenchikushi architect registered under standard law of Japan with experience on 
at least five similar projects. Evidence of extraordinary proven experience may be considered by the Contracting Officer as sufficient to act 
as the Quality Manager.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
<SPT outline="1.6.7.2"><TTL><SUB><pre class="display_SUB">&lt;SUB&gt;</pre>Field Testing Technician and Testing Agency<pre class="display_SUB">&lt;/SUB&gt;</pre></SUB></TTL><BRK />
<TXT>Submit data on qualifications of proposed testing agency and technicians for approval by the Contracting Officer prior to performing testing on 
concrete.</TXT><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">a. Work on concrete under this contract must be performed by an ACI Concrete Field Testing Technician Grade 1 qualified in accordance 
with <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>ACI SP-2<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> or equivalent JCI Concrete Field Testing Technician. Equivalent certification programs must include requirements for written 
and performance examinations as stipulated in <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>ACI SP-2<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">b. Testing agencies that perform testing services on concrete materials including reinforcing steel must meet the requirements of <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JASS 5<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>
, <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS Q 1011<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>, <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS Q 17011<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> and <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS Q 17025<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>.</LST><BRK /></SPT>
</SPT><SPT outline="1.6.8"><TTL>Laboratory Qualifications for Concrete Qualification Testing</TTL><BRK />
<TXT>The concrete testing laboratory must have the necessary equipment and experience to accomplish required testing. The laboratory must meet the 
requirements of <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JASS 5<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>, <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS Q 1011<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>, <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS Q 17011<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> and <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS Q 17025<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
<SPT outline="1.6.9"><TTL><SUB><pre class="display_SUB">&lt;SUB&gt;</pre>Laboratory Accreditation<pre class="display_SUB">&lt;/SUB&gt;</pre></SUB></TTL><BRK />
<TXT>Laboratory and testing facilities must be provided by and at the expense of the Contractor. The laboratories performing the tests must be accredited 
in accordance with <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS Q 17011<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> and <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS Q 17025<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>. The accreditation must be current and must include the required test methods, as specified. Furthermore, 
the testing must comply with the following requirements:</TXT><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">a. Aggregate Testing and Mix Proportioning: Aggregate testing and mixture proportioning studies must be performed by an accredited laboratory 
and under the direction of a Chief Concrete Engineer or Concrete Engineer authorized by the Japan Concrete Institute or First Class Kenchikushi 
who is competent in concrete materials and must sign all reports and designs.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">b. Acceptance Testing: Furnish all materials, labor, and facilities required for molding, curing, testing, and protecting test specimens 
at the site and in the laboratory. Furnish and maintain boxes or other facilities suitable for storing and curing the specimens at the 
site while in the mold within the temperature range stipulated by <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS A 1132<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">c. Contractor Quality Control: All sampling and testing must be performed by an approved, onsite, independent, accredited laboratory.</LST><BRK /></SPT>
</SPT><SPT outline="1.7"><TTL>ENVIRONMENTAL REQUIREMENTS</TTL><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: In some regions, designer must choose the most appropriate option(s) for ventilation. For instance, high-humidity 
regions may generate too much condensate when using 100 percent outside air.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<TXT>Provide space ventilation according to material manufacturer recommendations, at a minimum, during and following installation of concrete curing 
compound and sealer. Maintain one of the following ventilation conditions during the curing period or for 72 hours after installation:</TXT><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">a. Supply 100 percent outside air 24 hours a day.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">b. Supply airflow at a rate of 6 air changes per hour, when outside temperatures are between<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 13 degrees C<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 55 degrees F<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> and<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 29 degrees 
C<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 84 degrees F<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> and humidity is between 30 percent and 60 percent.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">c. Supply airflow at a rate of 1.5 air changes per hour, when outside air conditions are not within the range stipulated above.</LST><BRK />
<SPT outline="1.7.1"><TTL>Submittals for Environmental Performance</TTL><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">a. Provide SDS product information data showing that form release agents meet any environmental performance goals such as using vegetable 
and soy based products.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">b. Provide SDS product information data showing that concrete adhesives meet any environmental performance goals including low emitting, 
low volatile organic compound products.</LST><BRK /></SPT>
</SPT><SPT outline="1.8"><TTL>QUALIFICATIONS FOR WELDING WORK</TTL><BRK />
<TXT>Welding procedures must be in accordance with <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JASS 6<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>.</TXT><BRK />
<TXT>Verify that <SUB><pre class="display_SUB">&lt;SUB&gt;</pre>Welder qualifications<pre class="display_SUB">&lt;/SUB&gt;</pre></SUB> are in accordance with <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS Z 3881<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> for welding of reinforcement or under an equivalent qualification test approved 
in advance. Welders are permitted to do only the type of welding for which each is specifically qualified.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>

</SPT><SPT outline="2.2"><TTL>FORMWORK ACCESSORIES</TTL><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">a. Use commercially manufactured formwork accessories, including ties and hangers.</LST><BRK />

<SPT outline="2.2.1"><TTL>Form Ties</TTL><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: Form ties: a mechanical connection in tension used to prevent concrete forms from spreading due to the 
fluid pressure of fresh concrete.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">a. Use form ties with ends or end fasteners that can be removed without damage to concrete.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">b. Where indicated in Contract Documents, use form ties with integral water barrier plates or other acceptable positive water barriers 
in walls.</LST><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: Specify alternative breakback distance for ferrous ties if needed.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">c. The breakback distance for ferrous ties must be at least <div class="brackets">[<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre>50 mm<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre>2 in.<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG>]</div> <div class="brackets">[<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre>19 mm<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre>3/4 in.<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG>]</div> <div class="brackets">[_____]</div> for Surface Finish-2.0 or Surface Finish-3.0, 
as defined in <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>ACI 301<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>.</LST><BRK />
<div class="brackets">[<LST INDENT="-0.33">d. If the breakback distance is less than<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 19 mm<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 3/4 in.<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG>, use coated or corrosion-resistant ties.</LST><BRK />
]</div><LST INDENT="-0.33">e. Submit manufacturer's data sheet on form ties.</LST><BRK /></SPT>
<SPT outline="2.2.2"><TTL>Waterstops</TTL><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: waterstop: a thin sheet of metal, rubber, plastic, or other material inserted across a joint, or material 
adhered within a joint, to obstruct the seepage of water through the joint.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<TXT>Submit manufacturer's data sheet on waterstop materials and splices.</TXT><BRK />
<SPT outline="2.2.2.1"><TTL>PVC Waterstop</TTL><BRK />
<TXT>Polyvinylchloride waterstops must conform to <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS K 6773<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
<SPT outline="2.2.2.2"><TTL>Rubber Waterstop</TTL><BRK />
<TXT>Rubber waterstops must conform to <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS K 6773<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
<SPT outline="2.2.2.3"><TTL>Thermoplastic Elastomeric Rubber Waterstop</TTL><BRK />
<TXT>Thermoplastic elastomeric rubber waterstops must conform to <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS K 6258<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
<SPT outline="2.2.2.4"><TTL>Hydrophilic Waterstop</TTL><BRK />
<TXT>Swellable strip type compound of polymer modified chloroprene rubber that swells upon contact with water must conform to the following requirements 
when tested in accordance to <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS K 6251<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>: Tensile strength<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 2.9 MPa<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 420 psi<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> minimum; ultimate elongation 600 percent minimum. Hardness must be 
50:<div class="brackets">[40]</div> minimum on the type A durometer when tested in accordance with <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS K 6253<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> and the volumetric expansion ratio in distilled water at<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 20 degrees 
C<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 70 degrees F<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> must be 3 to 1 minimum.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
</SPT><SPT outline="2.2.3"><TTL>Biodegradable Form Release Agent</TTL><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: The 2002 Farm Bill - Section 9002, Federal Procurement of Biobased Products, requires each Federal Agency 
to develop a procurement program which ensures that items composed of biobased products are be purchased to the 
maximum extent practicable and which is consistent with applicable provisions of Federal procurement law.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">a. Provide form release agent that is colorless, biodegradable, and <div class="brackets">[rapeseed oil-based]</div> <div class="brackets">[soy oil-based]</div> <div class="brackets">[water-based]</div>, with a <div class="brackets">[low (maximum 
of 55 grams/liter (g/l))]</div> <div class="brackets">[zero]</div> VOC content.<div class="brackets">[ A minimum of <div class="brackets">[85]</div><div class="brackets">[_____]</div> percent of the total product must be biobased material.]</div></LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">b. Provide product that does not bond with, stain, or adversely affect concrete surfaces and does not impair subsequent treatments of 
concrete surfaces.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">c. Provide form release agent that reduces formwork moisture absorption, and does not contain diesel fuel, petroleum-based lubricating 
oils, waxes, or kerosene. Submit documentation indicating type of biobased material in product and biobased content. Indicate relative 
dollar value of biobased content products to total dollar value of products included in project.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">d. Submit manufacturer's product data on formwork release agent for use on each form-facing material.</LST><BRK /></SPT>
<SPT outline="2.2.4"><TTL>Chamfer Materials</TTL><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: Chamfer strip: either a triangular or curved insert placed in an inside form corner to produce either a 
rounded or flat chamfer or to form a rustication. Also called cant strip, fillet, dummy joint, and skew back.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />

<SPT outline="2.2.5"><TTL>Construction and movement joints</TTL><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: Indicate in Contract Documents the locations of required movement joints, keyways, and the locations where 
waterstops are required in joints.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>

<LST INDENT="-0.33">b. Locate construction joints within middle one-third of spans of slabs, beams, and girders. If a beam intersects a girder within the 
middle one-third of girder span, the distance between the construction joint in the girder and the edge of the beam must be at least twice 
the width of the larger member.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">c. For members with post-tensioning tendons, locate construction joints where tendons pass through centroid of concrete section.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">d. Locate construction joints in walls and columns at underside of slabs, beams, or girders and at tops of footings or slabs.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">e. Make construction joints perpendicular to main reinforcement.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">f. Provide movement joints where indicated in Contract Documents or in accepted alternate locations.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">g. Submit location and detail of movement joints if different from those indicated in Contract Documents.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">h. Submit manufacturer's data sheet on expansion joint materials.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">i. Provide keyways where indicated in Contract Documents.<div class="brackets">[ Longitudinal keyways indicated in Contract Documents must be at least<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 40 mm<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre>
 1-1/2 in.<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> deep, measured perpendicular to the plane of the joint.]</div></LST><BRK /></SPT>
<SPT outline="2.2.6"><TTL>Perimeter Insulation</TTL><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />

<LST INDENT="-0.33">f. Dimensional Stability (change in dimensions): 2 percent maximum.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">g. Water Vapor Permeance of 25 mm thickness: 200 ng/Pa&#183;s&#183;m<SPS>2</SPS>, maximum.</LST><BRK />
<TXT>Comply with EPA requirements in accordance with Section <SRF><pre class="display_SRF">&lt;SRF&gt;</pre>01 33 29<pre class="display_SRF">&lt;/SRF&gt;</pre></SRF> SUSTAINABILITY REPORTING</TXT><BRK /></SPT>

</SPT><SPT outline="2.3"><TTL>CONCRETE MATERIALS</TTL><BRK />
<SPT outline="2.3.1"><TTL>Cementitious Materials</TTL><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: Typical mixtures of concrete contain either an ASTM C150 cement plus one or more supplementary cementitious 
material (fly ash, slag, silica fume, etc.) or a blended cement that meets ASTM C595/C595M or ASTM C1157/C1157M.<BRK />
For more information on cements and cementitious materials refer to ACI E3 "Cementitious Materials for Concrete" 
and ACI 225R "Guide to the Selection and Use of Hydraulic Cements".<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE><NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: Coal fly ash, slag, cenospheres, and silica fumes are EPA designated products to be ingredients in concrete 
and cement. See Section <SRF><pre class="display_SRF">&lt;SRF&gt;</pre>01 33 29<pre class="display_SRF">&lt;/SRF&gt;</pre></SRF> SUSTAINABILITY REPORTING and include additive options unless designer determines 
that justification for non-use exists.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<SPT outline="2.3.1.1"><TTL>Portland Cement</TTL><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: ASTM C150 cements are as follows: <BRK />
- Type I: For use when the special properties specified for any other type are not required. <div class="brackets">[ASTM C150/C150 Type 
I or JIS R 5210 Ordinary Portland Cement]</div>.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>- Type II: For general use, more especially when moderate sulfate resistance is desired. <div class="brackets">[ASTM C150/C150 Type 
II or JIS R 5210 Moderate Sulfate Resistance Portland Cement]</div>.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>- Type II(MH): For general use, more especially when<BRK />
moderate heat of hydration and moderate sulfate resistance are desired. <div class="brackets">[ASTM C150/C150 Type II(MH) or JIS R 5210 
Moderate Heat and Sulfate Resistance Portland Cement]</div>.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>- Type III: For use when high early strength is desired.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>- Type III cement is not commonly used for cast-in-place concrete. It is a cement mostly available and used in 
precast operations. Type III could be used if high early strength is desired but using it will significantly 
increase the likelihood of thermal cracking. Type III cement should not be specified for flatwork.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>- Type IV cement (low heat of hydration) is not listed as an option because it is usually not produced by cement 
plants and is not available in U.S markets. A combination of Type II(MH) and a supplementary cementitious material 
such as fly ash is typically specified when low heat of hydration is required for a structure/member.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre> - Type V cement is a sulfate resistant cement. Refer to the paragraph on SULFATE RESISTANCE (under durability) 
for more information on when to specify sulfate resistant cement.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>Low-alkali cement could be specified; specifying it however, is not sufficient to mitigate ASR. To mitigate ASR, 
refer to the paragraph titled ALKALI-AGGREGATE REACTION.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>Type I cement is the default option. Commercially available cements can sometimes meet the requirements of Type 
I and Type II cements. These cements are labeled as Type I/II cements.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>JIS R 5210 standard defines various types of Portland Cement, such as: ordinary, high-early strength, ultra high-early 
strength, moderate-heat or sulfate resistant. Specify the type of cement as defined in JIS R 5210 that corresponds 
to ASTM C150 Type Cement that is required for the project if other than Type I.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">a. Unless otherwise specified, provide cement that conforms to <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS R 5210<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>, Ordinary Portland Cement <div class="brackets">[and meets <div class="brackets">[low alkali content requirements]</div><div class="brackets">[_____]</div>.]</div></LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">b. Use one brand and type of cement for formed concrete having exposed-to-view finished surfaces.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">c. Submit information along with evidence demonstrating compliance with referenced standards. Submittals must include types of cementitious 
materials, manufacturing locations, shipping locations, and certificates showing compliance.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">d. Cementitious materials must be stored and kept dry and free from contaminants.</LST><BRK /></SPT>
<div class="brackets">[<SPT outline="2.3.1.2"><TTL>Blended Cements</TTL><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: There are many options to choose from in ASTM C595. Here are some naming designations used:<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>- IP: portland-pozzolan cement<BRK />
- IS: portland blast-furnace slag cement<BRK />
- MS: moderate sulfate resistance<BRK />
- HS: high sulfate resistance<BRK />
- MH: moderate heat of hydration<BRK />
- LH: low heat of hydration<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>JIS blended cements include the following:<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>- JIS R 5211 Portland blast furnace slag cement. Blast furnace slag (Percent): Type A, more than 5 less than 
30; Type B, more than 30 less than 60; Type C more than 60 less than 70.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>- JIS R 5212 Portland pozzolan cement. Silica mixture (percent mass): Type A, more than 5 less than 10; Type B, 
more than 10 less than 20; Type C, more than 20 less than 30.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>- JIS R 5213 Portland fly ash cement. Fly Ash (percent mass): Type A, more than 5 less than 10; Type B, more than 
10 less than 20; Type C, more than 20 less than 30.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>Fly ash, silica fume, slag, and other SCMs may produce uneven discoloration of the concrete during the early stages 
of construction, depending upon the type of curing provided.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>Using Class C fly ash is not recommended, Class F fly ash is preferred. ASTM C595 describes Class C fly ash as 
typically produced from burning lignite or subbituminous coal and describes Class F fly ash as typically produced 
from burning anthracite or bituminous coal. The performance of Class C ashes should be evaluated before use because 
some Class C ashes could help improve performance while others could cause a reduction in concrete quality and 
durability. For example, some Class C fly ashes may improve sulfate resistance, while others may actually reduce 
sulfate resistance and accelerate deterioration. Class C should not be used to mitigate ASR unless mortar bars 
made with the fly ash meet the expansion requirements of ASTM C1567. For more information on the use of fly ash 
in concrete refer to ACI 232.2R.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>The conventional JIS A 6201 fly ash is Type II and is considered similar to ASTM C618 Class C and Class F, based 
on the following properties:<BRK />
- Ignition loss (percent): 5.0 or less<BRK />
- Fineness, Residue of 45 &#236;m sieve: 40 or less<BRK />
- Flow value ratio (percent): 95 or over<BRK />
- Activity index (percent): 80 or over<BRK />
- Silicon dioxide (percent): 45.0 or over<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>It is unknown what type coal JIS Type II fly ash is derived from.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE><BRK />
<TXT>Blended cements must conform to <div class="brackets">[<RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS R 5211<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>, Type <div class="brackets">[A]</div> <div class="brackets">[B]</div> <div class="brackets">[C]</div>]</div>, <div class="brackets">[<RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS R 5212<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>, Type <div class="brackets">[A]</div> <div class="brackets">[B]</div> <div class="brackets">[C]</div>]</div>, <div class="brackets">[<RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS R 5213<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>, Type <div class="brackets">[A]</div> <div class="brackets">[B]</div> <div class="brackets">[C]</div>]</div>.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
]</div></SPT><SPT outline="2.3.2"><TTL><SUB><pre class="display_SUB">&lt;SUB&gt;</pre>Water<pre class="display_SUB">&lt;/SUB&gt;</pre></SUB></TTL><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">a. Water or ice must comply with the requirements of <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS A 5308<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>, Annex C.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">b. Minimize the amount of water in the mix. Improve workability by adjusting the grading of the aggregate and using admixture rather 
than by adding water.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">c. Water must be <div class="brackets">[potable]</div> <div class="brackets">[from rainwater collection]</div> <div class="brackets">[from graywater]</div> <div class="brackets">[from recycled water]</div>; free from injurious amounts of oils, acids, 
alkalis, salts, organic materials, or other substances deleterious to concrete.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">d. Protect mixing water and ice from contamination during storage and delivery.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">e. Submit test report showing water complies with <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS A 5308<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>, Annex C.</LST><BRK />
<div class="brackets">[<LST INDENT="-0.33">f. When nonpotable source is proposed for use, submit documentation on effects of water on strength and setting time in compliance with <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>
JIS A 5308<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>, Annex C.</LST><BRK />
]</div></SPT><SPT outline="2.3.3"><TTL>Aggregate</TTL><BRK />
<SPT outline="2.3.3.1"><TTL>Normal-Weight Aggregate</TTL><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: ASTM C33/C33M provides many requirements for concrete aggregates. Requirements such as soundness and the 
presence of deleterious substances should strictly be adhered to. Grading requirements on the other hand could 
be evaluated based on the overall mixture design and not based on each individual aggregate source.<BRK /><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR>
<BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>Aggregate grading can be evaluated using methods such as 0.45 power chart, the coarseness factor chart, the "percent 
retained" or "18-8" method, and others. Quality concrete can be produced without meeting the grading requirements 
of ASTM C33/33M.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">a. Aggregates must conform to <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS A 5005<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> <div class="brackets">[unless otherwise specified in the Contract Documents or approved by the contracting officer]</div><div class="brackets">[_____]</div>.</LST><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: Specify a nominal maximum size aggregate if needed. Note that the maximum size aggregate can differ for 
different portions of the structure.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>Nominal Maximum Size: the smallest sieve opening through which the entire amount of the aggregate is permitted 
to pass.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>Delete the requirement below if you do not want to specify a maximum size aggregate. Note that the paragraph 
titled CONCRETE MIX DESIGN limits the nominal maximum size of aggregate based on the dimension of a member and 
spacing of reinforcement.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">b. Aggregates used in concrete must be obtained from the same sources and have the same size range as aggregates used in concrete represented 
by submitted field test records or used in trial mixtures.</LST><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: Calcium carbonate sands (limestone or dolomitic limestone) are softer than siliceous sands; when subject 
to abrasion, limestone sands in concrete polish and cause skid problems. To ensure that soft manufactured calcium 
carbonate sands are blended with harder sands (such as a natural siliceous sands), a 50 percent acid insoluble 
sand requirement must be specified when concrete is subject to abrasion (ex: pavements).<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>Note that for blended sands, the limit is for the blend of sand and not for each individual source of sand. Concrete 
produced with manufactured sands might require a higher w/c ratio, higher cement content, or higher admixture 
dosages to obtained the required workability and instability; Most hardened concrete properties (strength and 
durability) however will not be affected by the usage of 100 percentmanufactured sand. If finishability is an 
issue, then consider specifying 50 percent natural sand.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">c. Store and handle aggregate in a manner that will avoid segregation and prevents contamination by other materials or other sizes of 
aggregates. Store aggregates in locations that will permit them to drain freely. Do not use aggregates that contain frozen lumps.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">d. Submit types, pit or quarry locations, producers' names, aggregate supplier statement of compliance with <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS A 5005<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> and <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS A 1804<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> 
expansion data not more than 18 months old.</LST><BRK /></SPT>
</SPT><SPT outline="2.3.4"><TTL>Admixtures</TTL><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: There are 4 main classes of admixtures for concrete:<BRK />
- Water Reducers: Used to reduce the quantity of mixing water required to produce concrete of a given consistency.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>- Set Control: to retard or accelerate concrete setting time.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>- Durability Enhancing: to enhance the durability of concrete. These include air entraining admixture, corrosion 
inhibitors, ASR inhibitors, Shrinkage reducers, and others.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>- Miscellaneous admixtures: these include coloring admixtures, foaming agents, viscosity modifiers, etc.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>Specifying water reducers or set control admixtures is not necessary. The contractor should choose the combination 
of these admixtures as needed and as recommended by the admixture manufacturer. Air-entraining admixture dosage 
is controlled by the air content requirements specified in the paragraph titled DURABILITY. Thus, the specifier 
does not need to specify when an air-entraining admixture should be used. Other specialty admixtures however, 
such as corrosion inhibitors, ASR inhibitors, or shrinkage reducers should be specified in this paragraph if needed.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>For more information on concrete admixtures refer to ACI 212.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">a. Chemical admixtures must conform to <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS A 6204<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">b. Air-entraining admixtures must conform to <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS A 6204<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">c. Chemical admixtures for use in producing flowing concrete must conform to <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS A 6204<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">d. Do not use calcium chloride admixtures<div class="brackets">[.]</div><div class="brackets">[ unless approved by the contracting officer.]</div></LST><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: A corrosion-inhibiting admixture provides supplemental corrosion protection, specify if such an admixture 
is required under exposure C1 or C2.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>An ASR-inhibiting admixture provides supplemental protection to concrete when reactive aggregate is used. Specify 
if the usage of ASR-inhibiting admixtures is required.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>Specify if, when, and where any other specialty admixtures are required. Note that such requirements could also 
be specified in the paragraph titled CONCRETE MIX DESIGN.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">e. Admixtures used in concrete must be the same as those used in the concrete represented by submitted field test records or used in trial 
mixtures.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">f. Protect stored admixtures against contamination, evaporation, or damage.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">g. To ensure uniform distribution of constituents, provide agitating equipment for admixtures used in the form of suspensions or unstable 
solutions. Protect liquid admixtures from freezing and from temperature changes that would adversely affect their characteristics.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">h. Submit types, brand names, producers' names, manufacturer's technical data sheets, and certificates showing compliance with standards 
required herein.</LST><BRK /></SPT>
</SPT><SPT outline="2.4"><TTL>MISCELLANEOUS MATERIALS</TTL><BRK />
<SPT outline="2.4.1"><TTL>Concrete Curing Materials</TTL><BRK />
<TXT>Provide concrete curing material in accordance with <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JASS 5<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> and <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>MLIT-SS Chapter 6<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>. Submit product data for concrete <SUB><pre class="display_SUB">&lt;SUB&gt;</pre>curing compound<pre class="display_SUB">&lt;/SUB&gt;</pre></SUB>s. Submit manufactures 
instructions for placement of curing compound.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
<SPT outline="2.4.2"><TTL>Nonshrink Grout</TTL><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: Some nonshrink grouts derive their nonshrink properties from an increase in volume of metal due to oxidation. 
Nonmetallic grout is specified, since appearance of oxidation is considered undesirable/unacceptable. Refer to 
ASTM C1107/C1107M for standard specification for packaged dry, hydraulic-cement nonshrink grout and edit/amend 
paragraph 2.4.2 as required.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<TXT>Packaged dry, hydraulic cement non-shrink grout, that is non-metallic, non-corrosive, non-bleed, with the following performance requirements when 
prepared using the highest water-to-solids ratio, maximum flow, or most fluid consistency at 23.0 plus or minus 2.0 degrees C:</TXT><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">a. Minimum compressive strengths: 7.0 MPa at 1 day; 17.0 MPa at 3 day; 24.0 MPa at 7 day; and 34.0 MPa at 28 day.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">b. Early height change (maximum percent at time of final setting): plus 4.0 percent.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">c. Height change of moist cured hardened grout: 0.0 to plus or minus 0.3 percent at 1-day, 3-day, 14-day and 28-day.</LST><BRK /></SPT>
<SPT outline="2.4.3"><TTL>Floor Finish Materials</TTL><BRK />
<SPT outline="2.4.3.1"><TTL><SUB><pre class="display_SUB">&lt;SUB&gt;</pre>Liquid Chemical Floor Hardeners and Sealers<pre class="display_SUB">&lt;/SUB&gt;</pre></SUB></TTL><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">a. Hardener must be a colorless aqueous solution containing a blend of inorganic silicate or siliconate material and proprietary components 
combined with a wetting agent; that penetrates, hardens, and densifies concrete surfaces. Submit manufactures instructions for placement 
of liquid chemical floor hardener.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">b. Use concrete penetrating sealers with a low (maximum 100 grams/liter, less water and less exempt compounds) VOC content. Submit manufactures 
instructions for placement of sealers.</LST><BRK /></SPT>
</SPT><SPT outline="2.4.4"><TTL>Expansion/Contraction Joint Filler</TTL><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: Performance requirements for ASTM D 1751 joint filler material and ASTM D5249 backer material is provided. 
Refer to following ASTMs and edit/amend paragraph 2.4.4 as required:<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>ASTM D1751 standard specification for preformed expansion joint filler for concrete paving and structural construction 
(nonextruding and resilient bituminous types)<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>ASTM D1752 standard specification for preformed sponge rubber, cork and recycled PVC expansion joint fillers for 
concrete paving and structural construction<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>ASTM D5249 standard specification for backer material for use with cold and hot-applied joint sealants in portland-cement 
concrete and asphalt joints.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<TXT>Preformed, bituminous joint fiber filler for concrete paving and structural concrete construction. Provide joint filler meeting the following performance 
requirements:</TXT><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">a. Density: 300 kg/m<SPS>3</SPS> minimum.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">b. Compression: The load required to compress the test specimen to 50 percent of its thickness before test shall not be less than 690 
kPa and not more than 5100 kPa. If the nominal thickness of the specimen is less than 13 mm a maximum load of 8600 kPa is permitted.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">c. Extrusion/Protrusion: Test specimen shall be compressed to 50 percent of its thickness before test with three edges restrained. The 
amount of extrusion/protrusion of the free edge shall not exceed 6 mm.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">d. Recovery: The test specimen shall be compressed to 50 percent of its thickness before test. The load shall be released immediately 
after application. At the end of 10 minutes after release of the applied load, the specimen shall have recovered to at least 70 percent 
of its thickness before test.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">e. Water Absorption: The test specimen when submerged under 25 mm of water shall absorb not more than 15 percent by volume in 24 hours 
for 10 mm thickness and over.</LST><BRK />
<TXT>Material must be 13 mm thick<div class="brackets">[, unless otherwise indicated]</div>. <div class="brackets">[and of a width applicable for the joint formed]</div>. <div class="brackets">[Backer material shall be closed 
cell, polyethylene foam material with a density between 20-45 kg/m<SPS>3</SPS>; Greater than 95 percent compression recovery; compression deflection 38 kPa; 
Greater than 160kPa tensile strength; and 200 degrees C heat resistance for hot applied sealants]</div>.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
<SPT outline="2.4.5"><TTL><SUB><pre class="display_SUB">&lt;SUB&gt;</pre>Joint Sealants<pre class="display_SUB">&lt;/SUB&gt;</pre></SUB> and Seals</TTL><BRK />

</SPT><SPT outline="2.4.6"><TTL>Vapor Retarder <div class="brackets">[and Vapor Barrier]</div></TTL><BRK />

<LST INDENT="-0.33">d. Puncture Resistance, <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS K 7124-1<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>: 475 g <div class="brackets">[1700 g]</div> <div class="brackets">[2200 g]</div>, min.</LST><BRK />

</SPT><SPT outline="2.5"><TTL>CONCRETE MIX DESIGN</TTL><BRK />
<SPT outline="2.5.1"><TTL>Properties and Requirements</TTL><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: Selecting concrete proportions involves balance among requirements for placeability, workability, finishability, 
strength, durability, density, appearance, economy of the resulting mixture, and other desired properties.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>Properties specified in this paragraph such as strength, slump, aggregate size, etc. will be used to proportion 
concrete mixtures and/or order ready-mix concrete. For more on ready-mix concrete see paragraph on READY-MIX 
CONCRETE and ASTM C94/C94M. Note that the required information for ordering concrete is discussed in section 
6 of ASTM C94/C94M.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">a. Use materials and material combinations listed in this section and the contract documents.</LST><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: A minimum cementitious material content limit for concrete is generally not required for most portions 
of a structure. In the case of floors/slabs, a minimum content of cement could be required to improve the finishability 
of the surface. A finishing crew might have a hard time finishing a surface made with a lean concrete mixture; 
in such cases a minimum content of cementitious materials should be required.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">b. Cementitious material content must be adequate for concrete to satisfy the specified requirements for strength, w/cm, durability, and 
finishability described in this section and the contract documents.<BRK />

<LST INDENT="-0.33">d. The target slump must be enforced for the duration of the project. Determine the slump by <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS A 1101<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>. Slump tolerances must meet 
the requirements of <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JASS 5<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> and <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>MLIT-SS Chapter 6<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">e. The nominal maximum size of coarse aggregate for a mixture must not exceed three-fourths of the minimum clear spacing between reinforcement, 
one-fifth of the narrowest dimension between sides of forms, or one-third of the thickness of slabs or toppings.</LST><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: Exposure Class F1, F2, or F3 are defined in the paragraph titled DURABILITY.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">f. Concrete must be air entrained for members assigned to Exposure Class F1, F2, or F3. The total air content must be in accordance with 
the requirements of the paragraph titled DURABILITY.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">g. Measure air content at the point of delivery in accordance with <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS A 1118<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> or <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS A 1128<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">h. Concrete for slabs to receive a hard-troweled finish must not contain an air-entraining admixture or have a total air content greater 
than 3 percent.</LST><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: Specify the properties and requirements needed for each portion of the structure. Note that the values 
given for the first entry "Footings" is an example to illustrate how this table should be used. Modify this table 
by adding or deleting information and rows as needed for your project.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>- Minimum f'c (compressive strength): Specify the required compressive strength value and age for each portion 
of the structure. The strength value specified should be based on the value used for structural strengths or 
durability requirements, whichever controls. The age (7, 28, 56, 90) should be specified based on the needs of 
the project. 28-day strength is most commonly specified (default age for compressive strength). 7-day strength 
is specified only when high early strength is required on a project. 56- and 90-day strength requirements are 
specified for mixtures with relatively higher contents of pozzolanic materials because these mixtures require 
more time to gain strength. A higher compressive strength may be required for durability considerations. For 
floors, the specified compressive strength f'c will generally depend upon the intended use and expected wear unless 
durability considerations dictate higher strengths. If the floor will be exposed to abrasive wear from early 
construction traffic, consider requiring a minimum compressive strength at 3 days of 1800 psi or higher. Refer 
to ACI 302.1R for guidance on compressive strengths to specify for various classes of floors.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>- Information on exposure categories can be found in the paragraph titled DURABILITY and Chapter 19 of ACI 318. 
Choose the exposure categories for each portion of the structure as needed. Note that F0, C0, S0, and W0 are 
exposure categories that have no additional durability requirements and could be considered as default values.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>- Misc. Requirements: Add any requirement or property other than compressive strength, including aggregate size 
or gradation, w/c ratio and/or air content (if either is different than durability requirements), slump limits, 
fiber dosages, etc. Note that the default information in this table is given as an example of information that 
could be added; the table must be modified by the specifier as needed.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>-For information on lightweight concrete see ACI 213R.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
 <AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">i. Concrete properties and requirements for each portion of the structure are specified in the table below. Refer to the paragraph titled 
DURABILITY for more details on exposure categories and their requirements.</LST><BRK />

<SPT outline="2.5.2"><TTL>Durability</TTL><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: Proportions required for durable concrete may take precedence over those for strength. Durability can 
be more important than strength to the overall performance of the completed work. Concrete should be proportioned 
to resist the effects of exposures that can deprive it of serviceability. Durability is related to strength, 
but is also affected by factors which strength alone does not indicate. Strength tests alone are not a good predictor 
of durability. Additional durability tests on concrete and its components could be performed to insure that durable 
concrete is produced.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<SPT outline="2.5.2.1"><TTL>Alkali-Aggregate Reaction</TTL><BRK />
<TXT>Do not use any aggregate susceptible to alkali-carbonate reaction (ACR) to reduce the potential of alkali-silica reaction (ASR). For each aggregate 
used in qualifying concrete mixtures, the expansion result of the aggregate and cementitious materials combination determined in accordance with <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>
JIS A 1146<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> must not exceed 0.10 percent at an age of 16 days.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
<SPT outline="2.5.2.2"><TTL>Freezing and Thawing Resistance</TTL><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">a. Provide concrete meeting the following requirements based on exposure class assigned to members for freezing-and-thawing exposure in 
Contract Documents:</LST><BRK />

 <COL STYLEID="s50" AUTOWIDTH="0" WIDTH="144.75" />

specified in place of the<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 35&#176;C<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 95&#176;F<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> limit.<BRK />

curing, or protection of the concrete after delivery to the purchaser.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />

the following information in addition to that required by <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS A 5308<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>:</TXT><BRK />

<LST INDENT="-0.33">b. Cement and supplementary cementitious materials content in<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 43-kilogram<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 94-pound<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> bags per cubic<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> meter<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> yard<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> of concrete</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">c. Maximum size of aggregate</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">d. Amount and brand name of admixtures</LST><BRK />

</SPT><SPT outline="2.6"><TTL><SUB><pre class="display_SUB">&lt;SUB&gt;</pre>REINFORCEMENT<pre class="display_SUB">&lt;/SUB&gt;</pre></SUB></TTL><BRK />

than 2 months, cover coated reinforcement with opaque protective material.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">c. Submit manufacturer's certified test report for reinforcement.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">d. Submit placing drawings showing fabrication dimensions and placement locations of reinforcement and reinforcement supports. Placing 
drawings must indicate locations of splices, lengths of lap splices, and details of mechanical and welded splices.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">e. Submit request with locations and details of splices not indicated in Contract Documents.</LST><BRK />

use of A706/A706M bars. <BRK />
Or acceptable ASTM A615 Grades 40 and 60 reinforcement or JIS G 3112 - Grade SD 295 for sizes D10 to D16; Grade 
SD 345 for sizes D19 to D25, and Grade SD390 for Sizes D29 and larger that also meets these ACI 318 requirements: 
a) The actual yield strength based on mill tests does not exceed fy by more than 124 MPa; and b) The ratio of 
the actual tensile strength to the actual yield strength is not less than 1.25.<BRK />

of 0.55 percent, with percentage of Carbon not exceeding 0.30 percent and percentage of Manganese not exceeding

bottom dowel surfaces.]</div></TXT><BRK />
]</div></SPT><SPT outline="2.6.7"><TTL>Welding</TTL><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: For Weldability: It is recommended that Engineer of Record include requirement for Carbon Equivalent (CE) 
limit of 0.55 percent, with percentage of Carbon not exceeding 0.30 percent and percentage of Manganese not exceeding
