<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<div class="brackets">[<LST INDENT="-0.33">e. Sawcutting will be limited to within 12 hours after set and at 1/4 slab depth.</LST><BRK />
]</div></SPT><SPT outline="3.11.4"><TTL>Sealing Joints in Slabs on Ground</TTL><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">a. Contraction and control joints which are to receive finish flooring material must be sealed with joint sealing compound after concrete 
curing period. Slightly underfill groove with joint sealing compound to prevent extrusion of compound. Remove excess material as soon 
after sealing as possible.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">b. Sealed groove must be left ready to receive filling material that is provided as part of finish floor covering work.</LST><BRK /></SPT>
</SPT><SPT outline="3.12"><TTL>CONCRETE FLOOR TOPPING</TTL><BRK />
<SPT outline="3.12.1"><TTL>Standard Floor Topping</TTL><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: When standard floor topping is specifically required, the location of standard floor topping must be indicated.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<TXT>Provide topping for treads and platforms of metal steel stairs and elsewhere as indicated.</TXT><BRK />
<SPT outline="3.12.1.1"><TTL>Preparations Prior to Placing</TTL><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">a. When topping is placed on a green concrete base slab, screed surface of base slab to a level not more than<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 40 mm<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 1-1/2 inches<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> nor less 
than<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 25 mm<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 1 inch<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> below required finish surface. Remove water and laitance from surface of base slab before placing topping mixture. 
As soon as water ceases to rise to surface of base slab, place topping.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">b. When topping is placed on a hardened concrete base slab, remove dirt, loose material, oil, grease, asphalt, paint, and other contaminants 
from base slab surface, leaving a clean surface. Prior to placing topping mixture,<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 64 mm<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 2-1/2-inches<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> minimum, slab surface must be dampened 
and left free of standing water. Immediately before topping mixture is placed, broom a coat of neat cement grout onto surface of slab. 
Do not allow cement grout to set or dry before topping is placed.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">c. When topping is placed on a metal surface, such as metal pans for steel stairs, remove dirt, loose material, oil, grease, asphalt, 
paint, and other contaminants from metal surface.</LST><BRK /></SPT>
<SPT outline="3.12.1.2"><TTL>Placing</TTL><BRK />
<TXT>Spread standard topping mixture evenly on previously prepared base slab or metal surface, brought to correct level with a straightedge, and struck 
off. Topping must be consolidated, floated, checked for trueness of surface, and refloated as specified for float finish.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
<SPT outline="3.12.1.3"><TTL>Finishing</TTL><BRK />
<TXT>Give trowel finish standard floor topping surfaces.</TXT><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: Standard floor topping surfaces requiring an applied finish such as a chemical-hardener, non-slip aggregate 
finish, colored wear-resistant finish, sealers, or heavy-duty, wear-resistant finish must be indicated.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<TXT>Give other finishes standard floor topping surfaces as indicated.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
</SPT></SPT><SPT outline="3.13"><TTL>CURING AND PROTECTION</TTL><BRK />
<TXT>Curing and protection in accordance with <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JASS 5<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> and <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>MLIT-SS Chapter 6<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>, unless otherwise specified. Begin curing immediately following form removal. 
Avoid damage to concrete from vibration created by blasting, pile driving, movement of equipment in the vicinity, disturbance of formwork or protruding 
reinforcement, and any other activity resulting in ground vibrations. Protect concrete from injurious action by sun, rain, flowing water, frost, 
mechanical injury, tire marks, and oil stains. Do not allow concrete to dry out from time of placement until the expiration of the specified curing 
period. Do not use membrane-forming compound on surfaces where appearance would be objectionable, on any surface to be painted, where coverings 
are to be bonded to the concrete, or on concrete to which other concrete is to be bonded. If forms are removed prior to the expiration of the 
curing period, provide another curing procedure specified herein for the remaining portion of the curing period. Provide moist curing for those 
areas receiving liquid chemical sealer, hardener, or epoxy coating. Allow curing compound/sealer installations to cure prior to the installation 
of materials that adsorb VOCs, including <div class="brackets">[_____]</div>.</TXT><BRK />
<SPT outline="3.13.1"><TTL>Curing Periods</TTL><BRK />
<TXT><RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JASS 5<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> and <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>MLIT-SS Chapter 6<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>, except 10 days for retaining walls, pavement or chimneys. Begin curing immediately after placement. Protect concrete 
from premature drying, excessively hot temperatures, and mechanical injury; and maintain minimal moisture loss at a relatively constant temperature 
for the period necessary for hydration of the cement and hardening of the concrete. The materials and methods of curing are subject to approval 
by the Contracting Officer.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
<SPT outline="3.13.2"><TTL>Curing Formed Surfaces</TTL><BRK />
<TXT>Accomplish curing of formed surfaces, including undersurfaces of girders, beams, supported slabs, and other similar surfaces by moist curing with 
forms in place for full curing period or until forms are removed. If forms are removed before end of curing period, accomplish final curing of 
formed surfaces by any of the curing methods specified above, as applicable.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
<SPT outline="3.13.3"><TTL>Curing Unformed Surfaces</TTL><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">a. Accomplish initial curing of unformed surfaces, such as monolithic slabs, floor topping, and other flat surfaces, by membrane curing.</LST><BRK />
<div class="brackets">[<LST INDENT="-0.33">b. Accomplish final curing of unformed surfaces by any of curing methods specified, as applicable.</LST><BRK />
]</div><LST INDENT="-0.33">c. Accomplish final curing of concrete surfaces to receive liquid floor hardener of finish flooring by moisture-retaining cover curing.</LST><BRK /></SPT>
<SPT outline="3.13.4"><TTL>Temperature of Concrete During Curing</TTL><BRK />
<TXT>When temperature of atmosphere is<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 5 degrees C<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 41 degrees F<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> and below, maintain temperature of concrete at not less than<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 13 degrees C<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 55 degrees 
F<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> throughout concrete curing period or<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 7 degrees C<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 45 degrees F<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> when the curing period is measured by maturity. When necessary, make arrangements 
before start of concrete placing for heating, covering, insulation, or housing as required to maintain specified temperature and moisture conditions 
for concrete during curing period.</TXT><BRK />
<TXT>When the temperature of atmosphere is<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 27 degrees C<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 80 degrees F<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> and above or during other climatic conditions which cause too rapid drying of concrete, 
make arrangements before start of concrete placing for installation of wind breaks, of shading, and for fog spraying, wet sprinkling, or moisture-retaining 
covering of light color as required to protect concrete during curing period.</TXT><BRK />
<TXT>Changes in temperature of concrete must be uniform and not exceed<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 3 degrees C<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 37 degrees F<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> in any 1 hour nor<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 27 degrees C<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 80 degrees F<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> in any 24-hour 
period.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
<SPT outline="3.13.5"><TTL>Protection from Mechanical Injury</TTL><BRK />
<TXT>During curing period, protect concrete from damaging mechanical disturbances, particularly load stresses, heavy shock, and excessive vibration 
and from damage caused by rain or running water.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
<SPT outline="3.13.6"><TTL>Protection After Curing</TTL><BRK />
<TXT>Protect finished concrete surfaces from damage by construction operations.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
</SPT><SPT outline="3.14"><TTL>FIELD QUALITY CONTROL</TTL><BRK />
<SPT outline="3.14.1"><TTL>Sampling</TTL><BRK />
<TXT><RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS A 1115<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>. <TST>Collect samples of fresh concrete to perform tests specified.</TST> <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS A 1132<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> for making test specimens.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
<SPT outline="3.14.2"><TTL>Testing</TTL><BRK />
<SPT outline="3.14.2.1"><TTL><SUB><pre class="display_SUB">&lt;SUB&gt;</pre>Slump Tests<pre class="display_SUB">&lt;/SUB&gt;</pre></SUB></TTL><BRK />
<TXT><RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS A 1101<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>. <TST>Take concrete samples during concrete placement/discharge.</TST> The maximum slump may be increased as specified with the addition of an 
approved admixture provided that the water-cementitious material ratio is not exceeded. Perform tests at commencement of concrete placement, when 
test cylinders are made, and for each batch (minimum) or every<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 16 cubic meters<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 20 cubic yards<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> (maximum) of concrete.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
<SPT outline="3.14.2.2"><TTL>Temperature Tests</TTL><BRK />
<TXT><TST>Test the concrete delivered and the concrete in the forms</TST>. Perform tests in hot or cold weather conditions <MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre>(below 10 degrees C and above 27 degrees 
C)<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre>below 50 degrees F and above 80 degrees F<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> for each batch (minimum) or every<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 16 cubic meters<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 20 cubic yards<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> (maximum) of concrete, until the specified 
temperature is obtained, and whenever test cylinders and slump tests are made.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
<SPT outline="3.14.2.3"><TTL><SUB><pre class="display_SUB">&lt;SUB&gt;</pre>Compressive Strength Tests<pre class="display_SUB">&lt;/SUB&gt;</pre></SUB></TTL><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: When the same mix design is used for multiple elements such as slabs, beams, and walls, the design element 
type may be specified in lieu of or in addition to the mix design in order to better identify deficient concrete.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>Use eight cylinders when specifying 56 or 90 day strengths. Use 6x12 cylinders for better prediction of strength 
and consistency.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<TXT><TST><RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS A 1108<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>. Make <div class="brackets">[six]</div> <div class="brackets">[eight]</div><MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 150 mm by 300 mm<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 6 inch by 12 inch<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> <div class="brackets">[<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre>100 mm by 200 mm<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre>4 inch by 8 inch<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG>]</div> test cylinders for each set of tests in accordance 
with <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS A 1132<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>, <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS A 1115<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> and applicable requirements of <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JASS 5<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> and <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>MLIT-SS Chapter 6<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>. Take precautions to prevent evaporation and loss of water 
from the specimen. Test two cylinders at 7 days, two cylinders at 28 days, <div class="brackets">[two cylinders at 56 days]</div> <div class="brackets">[two cylinders at 90 days]</div> <div class="brackets">[_____]</div> and hold 
two cylinder in reserve. Take samples for strength tests of each <div class="brackets">[mix design of]</div> <div class="brackets">[and for]</div> <div class="brackets">[_____]</div> concrete placed each day not less than once 
a day, nor less than once for each<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 75 cubic meters<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 100 cubic yards<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> of concrete for the first<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 380 cubic meters<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 500 cubic yards<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG>, then every<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 380 cubic 
meters<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 500 cubic yards<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> thereafter, nor less than once for each <MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre>500 square meters<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET> of surface area for slabs or walls. For the entire project, take 
no less than five sets of samples and perform strength tests for each mix design of concrete placed. Each strength test result must be the average 
of two cylinders from the same concrete sample tested at 28 days<div class="brackets">[56 days]</div> <div class="brackets">[90 days]</div> <div class="brackets">[_____]</div>. Concrete compressive tests must meet the requirements 
of this section, the Contract Document, and <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JASS 5<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> and <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>MLIT-SS Chapter 6<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>. Retest locations represented by erratic core </TST>strengths. Where retest 
does not meet concrete compressive strength requirements submit a mitigation or remediation plan for review and approval by the contracting officer. 
Repair core holes with nonshrink grout. Match color and finish of adjacent concrete.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
<div class="brackets">[<SPT outline="3.14.2.4"><TTL><SUB><pre class="display_SUB">&lt;SUB&gt;</pre>Air Content<pre class="display_SUB">&lt;/SUB&gt;</pre></SUB></TTL><BRK />
<TXT><TST><RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS A 1118<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> or <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS A 1128<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> for normal weight concrete. Test air-entrained concrete for air content at the same frequency as specified for slump 
tests.</TST></TXT><BRK /></SPT>
]</div><div class="brackets">[<SPT outline="3.14.2.5"><TTL><SUB><pre class="display_SUB">&lt;SUB&gt;</pre>Unit Weight of Structural Concrete<pre class="display_SUB">&lt;/SUB&gt;</pre></SUB></TTL><BRK />
<TXT><RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS A 1116<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>. <TST>Determine unit weight of normal weight concrete.</TST> Perform test for every<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 15 cubic meters<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 20 cubic yards<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> maximum.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
]</div><div class="brackets">[<SPT outline="3.14.2.6"><TTL><SUB><pre class="display_SUB">&lt;SUB&gt;</pre>Chloride Ion Concentration<pre class="display_SUB">&lt;/SUB&gt;</pre></SUB></TTL><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: Include only when justified by size of job or when quality of concrete is questionable.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<TXT>Chloride ion concentration must meet the requirements of the paragraph titled CORROSION AND CHLORIDE CONTENT. <TST>Determine water soluble ion concentration 
in accordance with <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS A 1154<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>.</TST> Perform test once for each mix design.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
]</div><SPT outline="3.14.2.7"><TTL>Strength of Concrete Structure</TTL><BRK />
<TXT>The strength of the concrete structure will be considered to be deficient if any of the following conditions are identified:</TXT><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">a. Failure to meet compressive strength tests as evaluated.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">b. Reinforcement not conforming to requirements specified.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">c. Concrete which differs from required dimensions or location in such a manner as to reduce strength.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">d. Concrete curing and protection of concrete against extremes of temperature during curing, not conforming to requirements specified.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">e. Concrete subjected to damaging mechanical disturbances, particularly load stresses, heavy shock, and excessive vibration.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">f. Poor workmanship likely to result in deficient strength.</LST><BRK />
<TXT>Where the strength of the concrete structure is considered deficient submit a mitigation or remediation plan for review and approval by the contracting 
officer.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
<SPT outline="3.14.2.8"><TTL>Non-Conforming Materials</TTL><BRK />
<TXT>Factors that indicate that there are non-conforming materials include (but not limited to) excessive compressive strength, inadequate compressive 
strength, excessive slump, excessive voids and honeycombing, concrete delivery records that indicate excessive time between mixing and placement, 
or excessive water was added to the mixture during delivery and placement. Any of these indicators alone are sufficient reason for the Contracting 
Officer to request additional sampling and testing.</TXT><BRK />
<TXT>Investigations into non-conforming materials must be conducted at the Contractor's expense. The Contractor must be responsible for the investigation 
and must make written recommendations to adequately mitigate or remediate the non-conforming material. The Contracting Officer may accept, accept 
with reduced payment, require mitigation, or require removal and replacement of non-conforming material at no additional cost to the Government.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
<SPT outline="3.14.2.9"><TTL>Testing Concrete Structure for Strength</TTL><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: If the government is going to take cores and test them then include the bracketed paragraph.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<TST><TXT>When there is evidence that strength of concrete structure in place does not meet specification requirements or there are non-conforming materials, 
make cores drilled from hardened concrete for compressive strength determination in accordance with <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS A 1107<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID>, and as follows:</TXT><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">a. Take at least three representative cores from each member or area of concrete-in-place that is considered potentially deficient. Location 
of cores will be determined by the Contracting Officer.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">b. Test cores after moisture conditioning in accordance with <RID><pre class="display_RID">&lt;RID&gt;</pre>JIS A 1107<pre class="display_RID">&lt;/RID&gt;</pre></RID> if concrete they represent is more than superficially wet under 
service.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">c. Air dry cores, (<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre>16 to 27 degrees C<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre>60 to 80 degrees F<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> with relative humidity less than 60 percent) for 7 days before test and test dry 
if concrete they represent is dry under service conditions.</LST><BRK />
<LST INDENT="-0.33">d. Strength of cores from each member or area are considered satisfactory if their average is equal to or greater than 85 percent of the 
28-day design compressive strength of the class of concrete.</LST><BRK />
<div class="brackets">[<LST INDENT="-0.33">e. Core specimens will be taken and tested by the Government. If the results of core-boring tests indicate that the concrete as placed 
does not conform to the drawings and specification, the cost of such tests and restoration required must be borne by the Contractor.</LST><BRK />
]</div></TST><BRK />
<TXT>Fill core holes solid with patching mortar and finished to match adjacent concrete surfaces.</TXT><BRK />
<TXT>Correct concrete work that is found inadequate by core tests in a manner approved by the Contracting Officer.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
</SPT></SPT><SPT outline="3.15"><TTL>REPAIR, REHABILITATION AND REMOVAL</TTL><BRK />
<TXT>Before the Contracting Officer accepts the structure the Contractor must inspect the structure for cracks, damage and substandard concrete placements 
that may adversely affect the service life of the structure. A report documenting these defects must be prepared which includes recommendations 
for repair, removal or remediation must be submitted to the Contracting Officer for approval before any corrective work is accomplished.</TXT><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: Include this paragraph if the concrete structure is a water tank designed in accordance with ACI 530.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<div class="brackets">[<SPT outline="3.15.1"><TTL>Crack Repair</TTL><BRK />
<TXT>Prior to final acceptance, all cracks in excess of<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 0.50 mm<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 0.02 inches<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> wide must be documented and repaired. The proposed method and materials 
to repair the cracks must be submitted to the Contracting Officer for approval. The proposal must address the amount of movement expected in the 
crack due to temperature changes and loading.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
]</div><SPT outline="3.15.2"><TTL>Repair of Weak Surfaces</TTL><BRK />
<TXT>Weak surfaces are defined as mortar-rich, rain-damaged, uncured, or containing exposed voids or deleterious materials. Concrete surfaces with 
weak surfaces less than<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 6 mm<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 1/4 inch<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> thick must be diamond ground to remove the weak surface. Surfaces containing weak surfaces greater than<MET><pre class="display_MET">&lt;MET&gt;</pre> 
6 mm<pre class="display_MET">&lt;/MET&gt;</pre></MET><ENG><pre class="display_ENG">&lt;ENG&gt;</pre> 1/4 inch<pre class="display_ENG">&lt;/ENG&gt;</pre></ENG> thick must be removed and replaced or mitigated in a manner acceptable to the Contracting Officer.</TXT><NED /><BRK /></SPT>
<SPT outline="3.15.3"><TTL>Failure of Quality Assurance Test Results</TTL><BRK />
<NTE><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;NTE&gt;</pre><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK />
<NPR><pre class="display_NPR">&lt;NPR&gt;</pre>NOTE: Test results accomplished on concrete samples during concrete production that fall short of the acceptance 
criteria alert the Contractor to something in the production and placement process that has drifted out of calibration 
or that an error has been made. The goal is to track down the problem and correct it as quickly as possible. 
Unless the concrete producer makes a large error in batching or in placing, the chance that hardened concrete 
needs to be removed is remote. Removal and replacement is a last resort.<pre class="display_NPR">&lt;/NPR&gt;</pre></NPR><BRK />
<AST><hr></AST><BRK /><pre class="display_NTE">&lt;/NTE&gt;</pre></NTE>
<BRK />
<TXT>Proposed mitigation efforts by the Contractor must be approved by the Contracting Officer prior to proceeding.</TXT><BRK /></SPT>
</SPT></PRT> <END /><BRK /></SEC>
